### Round 1 | planner | planner_initial

- diagnosis: The task is to assess the likely AIE mechanism for a very large neutral hydrocarbon, C77H52. The current top1 working hypothesis is neutral aromatic, and the current runner-up is TICT. Additional credible portfolio members still requiring explicit screening are ICT and unknown. ESIPT is structurally non-credible because the molecule has zero hetero atoms and therefore no plausible proton-transfer motif. The top1 remains only a working hypothesis because the molecule also contains many peripheral aryl rotors, 10 rotatable bonds, and highly branched triarylethylene-like substituent topology, so a restriction-of-twisting picture could still compete with a neutral-aromatic locally excited picture. Shared prepared structure context is available and ready, including a selected conformer and geometry file, which supports a bounded baseline microscopic S0/S1 action. Macro can screen deterministic structural cues such as rotor topology or neutral-aromatic dominance, but it cannot decide the global mechanism. Microscopic can perform one low-cost baseline S0/S1 action and report state-localization/brightness-type cues, but in this first round it cannot cover conformer sensitivity, torsion sensitivity, or multi-step excited-state workflows. Because neither structure-only evidence nor one baseline excited-state snapshot is yet sufficient to eliminate all credible alternatives, the first round should gather both macro and microscopic evidence, and the case should remain in portfolio screening rather than pairwise contraction.

- task_completion_status: completed

- task_completion: Task completed successfully within current macro capability.

- task_understanding: The task is to perform a deterministic macro-level structural screening focused on rotor and torsion topology to assess the density of rotors, count of torsion candidates, branching and peripheral rotor patterns, and to evaluate the structural support strength for a twisted intramolecular charge-transfer (TICT) alternative versus a rigid neutral-aromatic interpretation. This must be done using the available shared prepared structure context without making any global mechanism decisions.

- reasoning_summary: Given the current hypothesis 'neutral aromatic' and the portfolio screening phase, the macro evidence so far supports a rigid aromatic core but leaves open the possibility of rotor-rich topology that could enable TICT. The recent microscopic evidence failed to provide direct charge-transfer descriptors, so the rotor/torsion topology screening is the next logical bounded structural discriminator to provide direct evidence on the presence and pattern of rotors and torsions. This will help clarify the local structural uncertainty related to TICT versus neutral aromatic interpretations without adjudicating the global mechanism.
Capability limit note: The macro capability is limited to deterministic low-cost single-molecule structural and topology analysis using the shared prepared structure context. It cannot perform excited-state relaxation, global mechanism adjudication, or aggregate-state modeling.

- execution_plan: Use deterministic_macro_structure_scan to execute the bounded registry-backed macro capability `screen_rotor_torsion_topology` with focus areas: TICT, unknown.
